[[वेदापौरुषेयत्त्ववादः	Source: [EB](https://www.ebharatisampat.in/read_chapter.php?bookid=ODY3NDcxNjgxMjE4MTAz)]]

\[














   INTRODUCTION  
    
  The Vedas and their contribution  
   to World Progress

 The Vedas are the fountain head of all knowledge from times immemorial. They have been handed down from generation to generations by oral tuition and their texts ate retained in different recensions, pure and untampered. It is Worth-while to know their extent and character in order to understand the role they play in moulding the life of man and leading him to his destined goal. In this general narration, the various attempts made by philosopher-scholars to interpret them and the divergent views expressed by the modern orientalists will be examined briefly in their proper context.  
   
 The Vedas as known to be the only guide book, indispensable to aspirants to know the mysteries of the Universe and the benign Hand (i.e.God) that controls them in reation to the capacities of the sentient and insentient beings that constitute it. The Vedic literature is known to be limitless (अनन्त). It was originally, i.e. in the krita Age, one undivided book and was called Mula Veda. In Treta age, it was divided into three divisions. Rik, Sama and Yajus and was called Upveda. In the Dvapara Age, Shri Vedavyasa arranged them into four divisions, Rik, Sama, Yajus and Atharva and called it Avantara Veda. Subsequently further smaller divisions came into being due to the incapacities of the students to study and understand them. The several Vedic Sakhas ar recensions now in vogue were the results of the attempts of the Vedic students is the kali Age, to study and interpret them.  
 ऋचः शाखात्वमापन्नः शिष्यतः शिष्यकैरिमाः।  
 संक्षेपं कृतवान्देव शिष्याश्च तदनुज्ञया ॥  
   Rik-Bhashya of Sri Madhvacharya  
 व्यदधाद्यज्ञसंतत्यै वेदमेकं चतुर्विधम्।  
 ऋग्यजुः सामाथर्वाश्च वेदाश्चत्वार उद्‌धृताः।




  Shri Gururajo Vijayate

  VEDAPAURUSHEYATVA VADA

   PREFACE

 The Present brouchure on the Vedas is an attempt to present to the student of ancient Indian (Bharatiya) culture, the interpretation of their contents by the traditional scholars by scientific analysis. The Vedas furnish the foundational knowledge on which the life and conduct of the Bharatadesha are shaped. The Vast mass of literature of different denomination: Tarka, Vedanta, Vyakarana, Chhandas, Dharmashastra etc., which forms the body of Indian literary talent is derived from the Vedas-directly or indirectly. Every act of an Indian is moulded so as to be conducive to the onward march to the gates of Happiness, from the Teachings of the Vedas and the Smritis including the Epics and the Puranas. This has imparted a spiritual glow unparallelled in the history of the world, to the Bharatadesha which is fittingly called as a "Veritable Workshop or show room of God's mysterious sports on Earth". Unfortunately, this spiritual aspect of Indian culture (Bharatiya Sanskriti) is side-tracked and missed by the modern students of the Vedas who relegate them to the level of chronicles of "Cock and Bull stoies and folk songs' collected in book form by the Pandits in different times and climes. The oriental Scholars of the last two centuries have distorted and descerated the sacred, lofty and transcendental character of the Vedic and Pauranic literature the fountain of universal inspiration by their materialistic approach and application of the so called \`historical method' of interpretation. They have built up round then, several \`sciences' such as anthropology, philology, Linguistics, Archaeology ect., which ply on the surface and do not dive deep into the mysteries of the Universe which lie beyond the ken of gross materialistic intellect.They stay away far from the \`grove of spiritual Bliss' and have landed an Indian Scholar in a wilderness to seek his destiny and struggle for existence in the midst of heterogenous forces that infest his life. The so called physical sciences are incompetent to lend any support to their fictitious arguements to detrect the transcendental vale of the Vedas.  
 It is, therefore, considered most desirable to re-assess the import of the Vedas and the Vedic literature by a fresh study of the original texts and presents our conclusions to the Scholars and the general readers so that they may revive the prestine glory of the Vedic culture the bed-rock of Indian life from times immemorial. As a first step in this direction, I have examined in this small study, the doubts and objections against the Vedas raised by the old and modern disputants and shown the hollowness of their stand in the words of the great thinkers and the Rishis who are accredited seers of divine dispensations. The homogenuity and unchallengeable spriti of the Vedic teachings of the Rishis is brought out with a scientific analysis.  
 It is proposed to issue a series of \`Studies' on the Vedas by surveying the Contents of the Samhitas, Brahmanas, Aranyaka and the Upanishads which constitute the stock of Vedic literature and tracing their influence on the later literature of the World. The Vedas are unhuman unrwitten store of knowledge handed down to humanity for their edification and onward march to the destined goal of unmixed happiness. I must acknowledge with gratitute that I have recieved valuable help from the works of Shri Madhvacharya the first great exponent of the Dvaita philosophy, the Tikas and Tippanis on them by Shri Jayatirtha, Vyasatirtha, Shri Raghavendratirtha etc. as well as from the writings of Naiyayikas, Mimamsakas etc. and Yaska, Kumarila Bhatta and Sayanacharya. The oriental Scholars like Roth, Whitney, Maxmuller, Winternitz and Macdonell and their followers have done a lot of work on the Vedas and ushered in a new approach of \`historical method' to unlock the hidden sense of the Vedas. The vast mass of literature produced by thses Scholars has almost shifted the secne of Vedic scholarship to the West. But, as I have stated above, their energies are misdirected in the sense that they have treated this sacred literture on par with the literary products of human intellect which is liable to grave defects. While admiring their zeal and tenacity to understand these sealed Books of knowledge, we are compelled to anounce that their results are unacceptable and suicidal to the march of spiritual progress of the world to which the Vedas are wedded.  
 I am conscious of the dangers of such an hazardous task. The modern scholars who are imbued with the so called historic methed of research, based on the theory of evolution in every branch of knowledge, will obviously cry hoarse against the theory of eternal truth preached by the eternal Vedas. But the fact can-not denied. God remains unchanging and eternal in the changing world of Prakriti and His commands, the Vedas which are coterminous with His etermal Mind are obviously eternal in their form and preaching. This is a very delicate problem which is beset with heavy controversy. I have explained in this brief treatise implications of this theory and hope that the Scholars will bestow their best attention on it and try to get convinced of the arguments set forth in the discussion.

 The Sanskrit part is based on the works of great authors and Philosophers of different Schools of thought. The English introduction summatises the discussion in Sanskrit and considers the views of the modern Scholars and puts them to critical test.

     R.S.Panchamukhi







   
 त एवमृषयो वेदं स्वं स्वं व्यस्यन्ननेकधा।  
 शिष्यैः प्रशिष्यैस्तच्छिष्यैः वेदास्ते शाखिनोऽभवन् ॥  
   -The Bhagavata

 "One undivided mass of the Vedas was made fourfold, to facilitate the performance of sacrifices. Then taking a portion from each division, the four Vedas Rik, Yajus, Sama and Atharva were created. Then, the sages divided their own sections of the Vedas into minor divisions and this practice was followed by their pupils, grandpupils and so on. Thus, the several recensions of the Vedas came into being. The main function of the Vedas is stated to be यज्ञसन्तत्यै i.e. for use in the sacrifices.  
 The sacrifice has to be attended compulsorily by at least four persons Adhvaryu, Hotri, Udgatri and Brahma, Prati-Prasthatri with Yajamana i.e.performer of sacrifice at the head. Hotri recites the Riks, Udagatar sings them (Sama) and Prati-Prasthatri narrates the action in prose (yajus). The services of another officer will be required in the arrangement and construction of the Vedic altar and Sthandilas and he must be well-versed in the Atharva-Veda where these details are described. Thus, all the four Vedas should be in active service in the celebration of sacrifices.  
 The auxiliary literature that aids the interpertations of the Vedic texts is called the Vedanga. It consists of शिक्षा (accents), कल्प (ritual), व्याकरण (grammer), निरुक्त (Etymology), छन्दः (prosody) and ज्योतिष (astronomy). The functions and use of the accents उदात्त, अनुदात्त and स्वरित which are preserved in the Vedas particularly Rig Veda even to this day in oral recitation are treated in the treaties called शिक्षा. The (rituals) ceremonial details which is the main part of sacrifice are given in the Kalpa. The knowledge of Vedic grammer (Vyakarana) is essential to understand the sense of the Vedic texts. Prosody (Chhandas) or the metre of the Vedic Mantras is again an important branch of knowledge which a student of the Vedas should necessarily possess. To add to these accomplishments, the science of astronomy (ज्योतिष jyotisha) must be studied to find out the auspicious Muhurta (day and time) when particular sacrifices have to be performed. Thus, the Vedangas help to furnish the preliminaries of the sacrifice. Thses are the extrenal aids to know the character and function of the Vedas. But the particular text of the Vedas enjoining particular sacrificical details have to be interpretted internally i.e. textually. What is the teaching of the Vedas ? This can be known only by the interpretation of the Vedas according to the accepted criteria of handling and funding out the import of the Vedas. They are the indispensable guides to the correct meaning and import of the verbal testimony in general. The same applies to the Vedas which constitute a special type of verbal testimony. Thses guides are well known principles defined in the Purva mimamsa of Jaimine Acharya and Brahma-Sutras of Badarayanacharya. Jaimine interprets the Vedas for the performence of sacrifices, according to these criteria. Similarly, Badarayana presses them into service to understand the sense of the entri Vedic lore.  
 उपक्रमोपसंहारावभ्यासोऽपूर्वता फलं ।  
 अर्थोवादोपपत्ती च लिंगं तात्पर्यनिर्णये ॥  
 श्रुतिर्लिगं समाख्या च वाक्यं प्रकरणं तथा ।  
 पूर्वं पूर्वं बलीयः स्यादेष आगमनिर्णयः ॥  
   
 Both the sets of five and four units have to be studiously and carefully employed to know the intended meaning of the Vedic or non-Vedic texts.

 Now, the Mimamsa (the science of enquiry) is two fold: कर्ममीमांसा and ब्रह्ममीमांसा. According to Jaimine, the entire Veda is dedicated to the teaching of \`action' (कर्म) only. Whereas Badarayana holds that it teaches ब्रह्म or Supreme God for whose knowledge कर्म has to be performed as a preliminary step, so that one can relise the futility of wordly कर्म which bring evanascient results, and cultivating the spirit of averstion towards short-lived worldly pleasure, can apply himself to know the Supreme God (Vishnu) who alone is capable of bestowing the eternal unmixed happiness or bliss upon the competent aspirants (अधिकारिन्). Jaimini the protagonist of karma is thus not antagonistic to the knowledge and devotion theory of Badarayana but only voices the view-point of such persons who are not fully qualified to adopt the knowledge-devotion course and have to train their mind by performing Karma and absolving the mind of all the roots of desire, and cultivating the spirit of renunction to worldly pleasures should adopt the knowledge course (ज्ञानमार्ग) which leads to the propitiation (प्रसाद) of God Vishnu. If one stops with the performance of Karma, he is undone. So, karma mimamsa is to be taken only as subsidiary to Brahma-mimamsa. This is the net resuly of the study of the Brahmamimamsa-Sastra. Shri Jayatirtha the celebrated commentator of the works of Sri Madhvacharya emphatically asserts, in the following passage the homogenity of the entire Vedas by explaining the functions of the Karma and knowledge (ज्ञान) texts in them.  
 The enquiry into the meaning of the Vedas and there by into the nature of the Brahman is Justified in the opening Sutra of the Brahma mimamsa Sastra Viz.  
 ॐ अथाऽतो ब्रह्मजिज्ञासा ॐ॥ अथ= अधिकारसंपत्यनंतरम् (after one is equipped with preliminary requisites of mental quietitude, aversion to worldy gains etc.)  
 अतः = मोक्षाख्यफलसद्भावात्, वेदस्य स्वतः प्रामाण्यात्,  
 बन्धस्य सत्यत्वात्, सिद्धार्थे व्युत्पत्तिसद्धावात्, ईश्वरप्रसादात्।  
 ॐ ब्रह्मणः = गुमपूर्णस्य विष्णोः (ब्रह्मणे = वेदार्थज्ञानाय)  
 जिज्ञासा कर्तव्या।  
 That the Sruti or Vedas provide requisite guidance for the attainment of bliss as stated in the oft-quoted Sruti text:  
 अदुःखमितरत्सर्वं जीवा एव तु दुःखिनः।  
 तेषां दुःखप्रहाणाय श्रुतिरेषा प्रवर्तते॥  
 The Advaitins hold that Sruti provides knowledge to remove the ignoramce about Brahman (God). The removal of ignorance amounts to self knowledge.  
 आत्मैवाज्ञानहानिः। अविद्यास्तमयो मोक्षः॥ i.e. Bilss is Moksha. Thus, the functions of the Vedas, according to the Vedantins (Sankara, Ramanuja and Madhva), is to give the knowledge of Brahman for the attainment of Moksha-though each differs in the conception of Brahman, Atman, Moksha etc., The Vedas are held by them to be Apaurusheya i.e. not created by Purusha = Man of God.  
 This view of Vedantins is controverted by the hereties headed by Charvaka, Bauddha, Arhat (Jain) by Naiyayikas and Agamikas also. The Mimamsakas and Samkhyas admit the authority of the Vedas but they explain their, while admitting their unquestioned authority, that they were composed by God who is Omniscient (सर्वज्ञः) and Supreme Creator of Universe. It is only the Vedantins who, after refuting the views of the heretics and other thinkers, establish the Apaurusheyatva (uncreatedness) of the Vedas and assign to it supreme authority in the domain of the extra sensuous problems, like Dharma, Adharma, Isvar, Svarga, Naraka, Papapunya etc,. Without entering into minute details of the problems I propse to give a brief summary of the arguments of the opposits schools of thought and the position of the Vedantins who refute them and establish their stand. The Charvaka (Atheist or upholder of physical pleasures-a-materialist) who admits only perception as the means of knowledge is brushed aside like God. sin, etc. Which cannot be denied. The Buddhist who admits Dharma etc., refutes the Charvaka tooth and nail and denounces him as an enemy of mankind (लोककण्टक). The Buddhists do not admit the aouthority of the word paurusheya or Apaurusheya, but declare that the word of Buddha is the fimal authority in matters not amenable to perection or induction (logic) inference. The Arhatas hold the same position but each controverts the other. The Mimamsakas and Vaisasikas refute the Buddhists and assert the infallibility of verbal testimony i.e.the Vedas. The Mimamsakas hold the vedas to be Apaurusheya wheras the Vaiseshikas take them to be the utterances of Isvara who is the supreme authority in all respects. The position of the Buddhists may be put forth as follows.  
 The Vedas are invalid, for they are hollow statements (अनृत), self-contradictory (व्याहत), repetitions (पुनरुक्त) meaningless (निरर्थ) and redundant (पुनरुक्त) since they are anticipated by other evidences: e.g.  
 (i) पुत्रकामः पुत्रकामेष्ट्या यजेत-One desiring to have a son should perform the sacrifice called पुत्रकामेष्टि. Though this is performed a son is not born. So, it is a false statement.  
 (ii) उदिते जुहोति अनुदिते जुहोति one should offer oblation at sun-rise and not at sun-rise, Self contradictory.  
 (iii) Repetition is found in the same text or in different recensions.  
 (iv) Fire is an antidote to cold. This is known by perception. Hence unnecessary. From thses specifice examples, the Entire Veda is proved to be unreliable and invalid.  
 This position is refuted by the Vedantin as follws: The non-yielding of fruit as stated ablove is due to other causes and not to the emptiness or falsity of the staement, for, when all auxiliary conditions are fulfilled the fruit as given in the text is found to have happed. The other arguments are similarly baseless, as repetitions etc. are designed to confirm the previous staments with greater emphasis.  
 Without an all round unquestionable validity of verbal testimaony, the extra-sensuous objects like Dharma, Adharma, Isvara etc. cannot be proved to exist. Such a word is Apaurusheya Veda, Which is beyond the teach of human deficiencies (पुरुषदोष). The Charvaka and Bauddha and in his train the Jaina etc. are set at rest, due to their inability to offer a solution since the first does not admit the extra seansuous objects which he is compelled to admit on his own ground and the latted who depend upon the reliability of Buddha as suprme authority, are unable to prove the omninscience of Buddha or Jina by perception or by inference. Their own Agamas cannot be acceptable by other philosophers unless they are proved to be authentic by some accredited evidence, which is not forth coming. Hence, for the proof of Dharma, Adharma, Virture Sin, heaven and hell which the buddisits also admit verbal testimony untouched by human failings is the only acceptable evidence. That is evidently to be Apaurusheya. To avoid the pit-falls of the Buddhists the logicians (Vaiseshiks etc). hold that such an authority is Isvara who is beyond the zone of human deficiencies such as अप्रतिपत्ति (ignorance) विप्रतिपत्ति (doubt) and अन्यथा-प्रतिपत्ति (error). But, how to prove the reloability of Isvara himself ? Hence, the only solution of this difficult maze is to admit the Vedas as Apaurusheya as otherwise Isvara would be charged with the grave offence of crurlty and partiality in awarding the fruit of action good of bad etc. to the Jiva.

 ॐ वैषम्यनैर्घृण्ये न सापेक्षत्वात्तथाहि दर्शयति ॐ।  
   -ब्रह्मसूत्रे 2-1-10-1  
 A question is put to the Vedantin. How to prove the validity of the Vedas ? Perception cannot function. In inference the minor premises i.e. the Anumana has to be known by some evidence. This again by some other evidence. Thus, it will lead to and in finitum (अनवस्था) which will end chaos. To this, the Vedantin replies that the instruments of knowledge and the knowledge produced by them are self-evident (स्वतः प्रमाण) and the Apaursheya Veda is self-evident. The Naiyayikas (Vaiseshikas) hode that the word (शब्द) is authentic, if it is uttered by a reliable person (आप्त) and since the Vedas, as the Vedantin says are un-uttered by any person, they are not authentic. This objection is met by the arguement that the intervention of Apta is ummecessary since at times the word of a cheat (प्रतारक) is by chance found to be true i.e. authentic. For a detailed exposition of this problem, the reader is requested to peruse the discussion in Vishnu Tatva-Nirnaya-Tika by Sri Jayatirtha, Anuvyakhana with Sudha Jignasadhikarana, Na-cilakshanatvadhikarana etc. of the Brahmasutras, a brief summary of the arguements if given in the Sanskrit Text below.  
 It is pertinent in this context, to know that the earliest literary evidences of high antiquity to prove the revelation of the vedas as Apaurusheya are available in the Nirukta of Yaska, Mimamsa-Sutra of Jaimini (I Chapter) with Vartikas of Kumarlia-Bhatta besides the Brahmsutras of Badarayana, with the Bhashyas of Sri Shankaracharya, Sri ramanujacharya and Sri Madhvacharya. A Volley of references can also be cited from the Vedas themselves and the Mahabharat, Puranas and the the incontrovertible tradition from times immemorial,  
 वेदास्ते नित्यविन्नत्वात् श्रुतयश्चाखिलैः श्रुतेः।  
 आम्नायोऽनन्यथापाठादीशबुद्धिस्थिताः सदा ॥ इति -महावाराहे  
 The very names वेद, श्रुति and आम्नाय defines the character of theis verbal testimony as being eternal or uncreated. Sri jayatirtha explain in his commentary of the passage in Vishnutatvanirnaya.  
 न चानित्यत्वे श्रुतिर्वेद इत्यादि विशेषशब्द उपपद्यते।  
   
 If this piece of evidence i.e. श्रुति is not all abiding (नित्य), the names. श्रुति, वेद and आम्नाय, unless they convery a specific sense, (असाधारण्येन व्यपदेशा भवन्ति) would carry no meaning. Why should Vedas be called by these terms when other words do exist (विद) (विद्‌=विन्न), are heard (श्रुत) and repeated (आम्नायः). The special feature intended is obviously their eternalmess which is uncommon with other words of purana Kavya etc. The order and sense of the letters and words in the Vedas are unchangeable and immuntable, and remain the same even during the Mahapralaya when they reat in the Mind of the od which is etermal. This citation from the purana Madhavaraha brings out the real nature of the Apaurushaya Veda. The following verses from the Brahmandapurana are more explicit.

 नित्या वेदाः समस्तश्च शाश्वता विष्णुबुद्धिगाः।  
 सर्गे सर्गेऽमुनैवैते उद्‌गीर्यन्ते तथैव च॥  
 तत्क्रमेणैव तैर्वर्णैस्तैः स्वरैरेव नाऽन्यथा।  
 All the Vedas are eternal and in the Mahapralaya, reat in the mind of Vishnu. The same are manifested by God at the beginning of next creation, the order of accents, syllables and words remaining unchanged. God Vishnu sees them and others hear them.  
 यतस्ता हरिणा दृष्टाः श्रुता एवापरैर्जनैः।  
 श्रुतयो दृष्टयश्चेति तेनोच्यन्ते पुरातनैः॥  
 Hence, they are designated as श्रुति and दृष्टि by the elders. Sri Jayatirtha adds \`न च नित्यत्वं विना दर्शनव्यवहारो युज्यते'। If a thing is to be seen, it must exsi always before, to, since God Vishnu sees it, it must exist. i.e. must be eternal. वेद is derived from the root विद् = to be, to exist. By the dictum असाधारण्येन व्यपदेशा भवन्ति, the existence or being must be taken, unlike in other cases, to be constant which ultimately gives the sense of eternalness.  
 In the Vedas we come across, statements converying a sense of their creation as e.g. ऋचः सामानि जज्ञिरे etc. The Sama Veda was born of Rik. Some of the Vedic texts ate known after the name of some ऋषि's. And some shapters are known after some duties like वैश्वानरविद्या, अग्निविद्या, पुरुषविद्या etc. Such references are explained in the same Purana as-  
 तदुत्पत्तिवचश्चैव भवेद् व्यक्तिमपेक्ष्य तु।  
 चेतनस्य जनिर्यद्वदुच्यते सर्वलौकिकैः॥  
 वेदानां सृष्टिवाक्यानि भवेयुर्व्यक्त्त्यपेक्षया।  
 नाऽनित्यत्वात्कुतस्तेषामनित्यत्वं स्थिरात्मनाम्॥ -ब्रह्माण्डे  
 The statament of "production" should be understood in the sense of manifestation, as in the ऋक्.  
 तस्माद्विरालजायत। स जातोऽत्यरिच्यत।  
 चन्द्रमा मनसो जातः। चक्षोः सूर्योऽजायत॥ etc.,  
 Or, it may refer to the birht of the deities \[i.e. their bodies\] presiding over the Vedas. In some cases the terms प्रत्न \[old\] and नूत्न \[new\] are with reference to the ऋषि's who have perceived the Vedas. This does not affect the eternal character of the Vedas, since the Vedas existing for all times in the mind of the God, flash to the mind of the sages old and new, by the grace of the God.  
 जन्मान्तरश्रुतास्तास्तु वासुदेवप्रसादतः।  
 मुनीनां प्रतिभास्यन्ति भागेनैव न सर्वशः॥ -ब्रह्माण्डे  
 The Vedas heard in previous births flash on the mind of the Munis in the next birht, through the grace of vasudeva. Hence, some of the Vedic passages go after the names of the seers like वसिष्ठ, वामदेव, गृत्समद, विश्वामित्र etc., Similarly काठक, कापालक occuring in the Vedic texts should be explained as being only indicative terms (उपलक्षण) for promoters, of the Sakhas, not affecting their अपौरुषेयत्व and नित्यत्व.  
 So far, the evidence of Purana was cited. Now the श्रुति itself gives out it nature in the passages like तस्मै नूनमभिद्यवे वाचा विरूप नित्यया। वृष्णे चोदस्व सुष्टुतिम्।  
 This mantra enjoins Virupa to extol the giver of boons by the eternal Vak (नित्यया वाचा). The पैंगीश्रुति explains that Nitya Vak (वाक्) is श्रुति and अनित्यवाक् is स्मृति  
 (श्रुतिर्वाव नित्या अनित्या वाव स्मृतयः याश्चान्या वाचः।  
     - इति पैंगीश्रुतिः)  
 The term नित्यवाक् in this passage means अपौरुषेय वेद by means of which, God Vishnu can be known as stated in the "Katyayana Sruti".  
 विज्ञेयं परमं ब्रह्म ज्ञापिका परमा श्रुतिः।  
 अनादिनित्या सा तच्च विना तां न स गम्यते।  
    - कात्यायनश्रुतिः  
 The श्रुति persists as long as Brahman with countless prooves lives i.e. is नित्य = imperishable.  
 सहस्रधा महिमानः सहस्रं यावद्‌ब्रह्म विष्ठितं तावती वाक्।  
 यश्छन्दसां योगमावेद धीरः को धिष्ण्यां प्रति वाचं पपाद।-श्रुतिः।  
 Thus, from the evidance of Purana and श्रुतिः in addition to the inference mentioned while refuting the buddhists, Arhatas and Vaiseshikas etc. it is established that the Vedas are Apaurusheya without which the extra sensuous objects cannaot be proved to exist. One may object to this sort of argument since a thing should be proved to exist by evidance and not presumed with the object of satisfying our requirement (मानाधीना मेयसिद्धिः। न प्रयोजनाधीना।). In the latter case, a thirsty man will hace to get water in a barren land to satiate his thirst (पिपासितस्य मरुभूमौ वारिसिद्धिः स्यात्।). To counter-act this objection advanced by the charvaka who admits only perception as the source of knowledge, the Vedantin cites the validity of verbal transaction in every day life which even the Charvaka should accept and on the analogy of it, the Purana and श्रुति evidance are produced. When verbal testimony is admitted, it is easy to prove the authenticity of the Agamas and Puranas for which the श्रुति becomes a primary authority.  
 In this context, a few minor queries require to be satisfactorily explained. In the Vedas, mention of persons like Harischandra, Janamejaya, yudhishthira etc., the inclusion of personal reference as I, You, He etc., and the associstion of personal factor, miltate against the Apaurusheyatva \[un-personal\] character of the Vedas. Passages which contain the praise or censure of practices (अर्थवाद) cannot be reconciled with the absence of personal elements. These and similar objections can be cleared by supposing that personal elements or praise and censure are of general application and do not refer to a particular individual or person, as in पापोऽहं पापकर्माऽहं etc., in which the expresstion अहं which applies to every person who utters it, is impersonal and so the similat experssions in the Vedas need not refer to the composer of the श्रुति. It is pointed out that the succession and order of words and syllables in sentences pre-suppose the function of human intellect and so the Vedas must be the productions of a thinking mind. Here again the order and successtion of words which are caused by the mind of Isvara (उपाधि) where they rest, are eternal as His Mind is eternal, though the same may be momentary when uttered or recited by the teacher and student of the Vedas in their daily recital since that mind are subject to change and are non-eternal.  
 नित्या वेदाः समस्ताश्च शाश्वता विष्णुबुद्धिगाः।  
 सर्गे सर्गऽमुनैवेते उद्‌गीर्यन्ते तथैव च।  
 तत्क्रमेणैव तैर्वणैः तैः स्वरैरेव नाऽन्यथा॥ -ब्रह्माण्डे  
 The letters (syllables) and words composed in them which imply the arrangement of letters in a particular order due to the mental exrcise, are also aternal since the Omniscient God's Mind where they primarily rest \[i.e. conceived\] is eternal.  
 न च वर्णपदादीनामनित्यत्वं वक्तुं युक्तम्।  
 सर्वज्ञत्वादीश्वरस्य तद्‌बुद्धौ सर्वदा प्रतीयमानत्वात्। (वि.त.नि)  
 Even during Pralaya, the Vedas and their order of words, letter and sense are not altered and they are transmitted as such by God at the next creation of the world, first to Chaturmukha Brahma \[four faced Brahma\] through whom they are spread among the gods and men. In the case of Puranas etc. however, which also rest in mind of God, the sense is mot changed at the mext transmisson, while the order of words etc., is changed; for example अग्निमीले पुरोहितं of the Veda remains en bloch constant in sense and in form, accent and order of the component words and latters wher-as the Anushtubh verse नारायणं नमस्कृत्य नरं चैवं नरोत्तमं fetc. of the Itihasa and Puranas (i.e. works composed by God or human authors) may change the order of words etc., in the next creations. This difference between the Vedas and Puranas etc., is stated to be a riddle to us for the present.  
 नन्वेवं वेदपुराणयोः नित्यत्वे पुराणानां पुनारचनं न वेदस्येत्येतत्कुत इति चेत्। प्रमाणप्रश्नश्चेत् उक्तादेव पुराणवाक्यादिति ब्रूमः। प्रयोजनप्रश्नस्तु अयुक्तः। ईश्वप्रवृत्तेः सर्वत्र स्वप्रयोजनरहितत्वात्। परप्रयोजनानि तु सूक्ष्माण्युत्प्रेक्षितुं वयं न प्रभवामः। भगवानाचार्योऽपि इदानीं प्रयोजनाभावात् नाऽवादीदिति।  
    (-वि.त.नि.टीका)  
 That the Vedas are Nitya (aternal) in the sense and composition of words etc., and are distinguished from the Puranas is maintained in the ancient literary works like Yasks's Nirukta and Sloka Vartika of Kumarila Bhatta (8th Cent. A.D.) on Jaimini-mimamsa-Sutras. Yaska puts in the mouth of Kautsa objections against the validity and revalation of the Bedas which anticipate the arguments of the Charvakas, Buddhists and Jains who reile the Vedas as concoctions of priest-craft deliberately designed to maintain the aggrandisement and superiority of the Brahman class.  
 Yaska the author of Nirukta introduces A questioner in the person of Kautsa who poses certain queries against the Vedas as infallible evidence, and argues that they are full of repetitions, conflicting and false statements, reduancies and enigmas etc.  
 यदि मन्त्रार्थप्रत्ययाय अनर्थकं भवतीति कौत्सः। अनर्थका हि मन्त्राः। तदेतेनोपेक्षितव्यम्। नियतवाचो युक्तयो नियतानुपूर्व्याः भवन्ति। अथापि ब्राह्मणेन रुपसम्पन्ना विधीयन्ते। अथाप्यनुपपन्नार्था भवन्ति।---अथापि विप्रतिपन्नार्था भवन्ति। अथापि जानन्तं सम्प्रेष्यति।---अथाप्याहाऽदितिः सर्वमिति। अथाप्यविस्पष्टार्था भवन्ति। इति।  
 All these objections are removed by Yaska in his replies:-

 1) अर्थवन्तः शब्दसामान्यात्।  
 2) यतो एतन्नियतवाचो युक्तयः नियतानुपूर्व्या भवन्तीति लौकिकेष्वप्येतत्।  
 3) यतो एतद्विप्रतिपत्तिसिद्धार्था भवन्तीति लौकिकेष्वप्येतत्।  
 4) यतो एतज्जानन्तं सम्प्रेष्यतीति जानन्तमभिवादयते। जानते मधुपर्कं प्राह इति।  
 5) यतो एतददितिः सर्वमिति लौकिकेष्वप्येतत्।  
 6) यतो एतदविस्पष्टार्था भवन्तीति नैष स्थाणोरयमपराधः यदेनमन्धो न पश्यति। पुरुषापराधः स भवति।  
   
 यथा जानपदीषु विद्यातः पुरुषविशेषो भवति। पारोवर्यवित्सु तु वेदितृषु भूयोविद्यः प्रशस्यो भवति ॥16॥  
 There is no special objection against the Vedic words which is not found in the लौकिक or profane usage, the order and sequence of Words in which, are admitted as meaningful and authantic. If one doesnot make out their meaning in such cases as अथ्यक्, यादृश्मिन्, जारयापि, काणुका etc., it is the fault of the scholar who is not equipped with the knowledge of Nirukta. Yaska ultimately declares that the Vedas are revalations i.e.seen (not composed) by the seers thorgh the Grace of God.:  
 साक्षात्कृतधर्माणः ऋषयो बभूवुः। तेऽवरेभ्योऽसाक्षात्कृतधर्मभ्यः उपदेशेन मन्त्रान् प्राददुः। उपदेशाय ग्लायन्तोऽवरे बिल्वग्रहणायेमं ग्रन्थं समाम्नासिषुः। वेदं च वेदाङ्गानि च।    -(नि.1-1-20)  
 Jaimini, in his पूर्वमीमांसासूत्र's explains the position of Yaska in greater details as follows:-  
 चोदनालक्षणोऽर्थो धर्मः। औत्पत्तिकस्तु शब्दस्यार्थेन सम्बन्धस्तस्य ज्ञानमुपदेशेऽव्यतिरेकश्चार्थेऽनुपलब्धे तत्प्रमाणं बादरायणस्यानपेक्षत्वात्।

and establishes the dicinity and revatation of the Vedas and states that they are eternal and unwritten (अपौरुषेय). He refutes the objections of the opponents who are introduced in the Sutras वेदांश्चैके संनिकर्ष पुरुषाख्या (as stafting that they are know after human beings) \[1,1,27\], अनित्यदर्शनाच्य \[1,1,28\] (and are connected with non-eternal things). They are replied in the Sutras उक्तं तु शब्दपूर्वत्वं (1,1,29) आख्याप्रवचनात् (1,1,30) and परं तु श्रुतिसामान्यमात्रं (1,1,31).  
 Yaska says that the word whether human or recealed is eternal and its connection with human beings in the Vedas merely shows that they were transmitters of the eternal words of the Vedas by oral tution (प्रवचन). The mention of certain names of human beings or places merely indicates that the names do not refer to specific proper persons or places but only to common nouuns. Sayana in his introduction to Rigbhashya summarises the the discusstion of the Hirukta and Jaimini Sutras of Purva-Mimamsa and as well as the Sloka Vartika of Kumarila Bhatta and elucidates the points by adding his own notes on them. Sayana observes that the Vedas are infallible, self-evident proff for Dharma and the references in them to non-eternal objects like names of persons, places and events are common names, or should be interpreted by atymological criterion (योग) to refer to common truths. In the Mantreadhikarana I, 2,31-53 all the objections of Kautsa in the Nirukta are considered and answered.  
 The Sutra अनितियसंयोगात् मन्त्रानर्थक्यम् (1,2,39) is relevent in the present context of the eternalness of the Vedas. In किं ते कृण्वन्ति कीकटेषु the name of the country कीकट is mentioned. Similarly the town Naichasikha and the king Pramangada are introduced. Thses and similar references in the Vedas obviously prove that they are not eternal but came into existence only after these objects were born. This doubt is removed in the Sutra उक्तश्चानित्यसंयोगः (1,2,50). In the Taittiriyasamhita (7,1,10,2) बवरः प्रावाहणिरकामयत the transitory names बवर and प्रावाहणि are found. The Sutra परं तु श्रुतिसामान्यमात्रं। removes the doubt by suggesting that these are not proper nouns but only common noums which are true for all times, past, present and future. In the Veda, Nityatvadhikarna, Kumarila Bhatta in his Slakavartika considers all the arguments of the opponent and concludes as in Nirukta that the mention of transitory objects does not conflict with the eternalness of the Vedas sinces they are common nouns abiding for all times. Bavara (बवर) is taken to be in imitation of the sound of wind and Pravahani as the gust of wind moving with great velocity.  
 वचनान्तरसाधर्म्यात्कर्तुः सामान्यसम्प्लवे।  
 समाख्यया विशेषोऽयं कठादिरवधार्यते॥  
 स्मृतिप्रयोजनाभावात्कर्तृमात्रेऽनपेक्षिते।  
 सामान्यसिद्ध्यपेक्षत्वात् न समाख्या नियामिका॥ श्लोकवार्तिक-वेदनित्यत्वाधिकरण  
 The mention of काठक and कापालक is not indicative of the transitoriness of the Vedas. Only the commonness of the name is intended. This can be explained otherwise also.  
 अन्यथा।़प्युपपन्नत्वादियं प्रवचनादिना।  
 न शक्ता कर्तृमूलाय प्रोक्ते च स्मरणे स्थितम्॥  
 The connection of transitory persons can be ascribed to tha fact that the particular Vedas were expounded by them and not composed. They are remembered becouse they were the first teachers of expounders to the world.  
 In addition to these arguments of Yaska, Jaimini, Kumarila Bhatta and sayana, the reader is invited to refer to the refreshing discusstion of this problem in the Brahmasutras of Badarayana. Where in chapter II 3,4 padas, the conflicting statements in Vedas have been reconciled on good textual Vedic authorities and the अपौरुषेयत्व and स्वतः प्रामाण्य (self-validity) of the Vedas has been established (see the न विलक्षणत्वाधिकरण). This unbroken stream of evidence treced from the ealiest literary works to the late 13,14th Cent. A.D. and continued upto date is supported by the Itihasa, Purana and Smriti etc., The Mahabharata is the epitome of the Vedas (भारतव्यपदेशेन ह्याम्नायार्थः प्रदर्शितः॥ Bhagavata, 1,4,27,28.). Bhagavata is the essence of Brahmasutra, Bharata, Gayatri, and the Vedas.  
 ब्रह्यसूत्रमहाभारतगायत्रीवेदसम्बन्धाश्चायं ग्रन्थः। -भागवततात्पर्य  
    -by Sri Madhvachrya  
 This is fully borne out by the Puranas. Garuda and Brahmanda. The Nirukta of Yaska commends that the Vedas should be interpretted with the aid of Itihasa and Purana. See also the Gita Bhashya of Sri Madhvacharya.  
   
 भारतं चापि कृतवान् पञ्चमं वेदमुत्तमम् ।  
 दशावरार्थ सर्वत्र केवलं विष्णुबोधकम् ॥  
 परोक्षार्थं तु सर्वत्र वेदादप्युत्तमं तु यत् । - इति स्कान्दे  
   
 यदि विद्याच्चतुर्वेदान् सांगोपनिषदान् द्विजः ।  
 न चेत्पराणं सांविद्यात् नैव स स्याद्विचक्षणः ॥

 इतिहासपुराणाभ्याम् वेदं समुपबृंहयेत् ।  
 बिभेत्यल्पश्रुताद्वेदो मामयं प्रचलिष्यति ॥  
 sayana adds  
   
 षडंगवत्पुराणादीनामपि वेदार्थज्ञानोपयोगो याज्ञवल्क्येन स्मर्यते।

 न्नपुराणन्यायमीमांसाधर्मशास्रांगमिश्रिताः ।  
 वेदाः स्थानानि विद्यानां धर्मस्य च चतुर्दश ॥ (I,3)  
   
 (See further, Sayana's Introduction to Rig Veda, Bhashya, P. 21-22 Maxmuller's edition, pulished by pasupati Ananda Gajapati Raj and Fredirch Maxmuller).  
   
 Thus, it is noticed that the self-validity, supreme anthority and the revatation of the Vedas are accepted by all philosophers in India from the remotest period of history upto the present time. A few rebles of the Vedic authority, the Charvaka, Bauddha and jain are far and few between and have been thrown into insignificance due to the weakness of their stand. All the Vedantins and the Naiyayikas, Samkhyas and the Agamika schools of Saivism have joined hands in refuting the revilers of the Vedas. Arthasatra, Nitisastra and other popular sciences like आयुर्वेद, धनुर्वेद etc., draw their materials from and depend upon the Vedas for their development. Thus, the authority of the Vedas as a revealed doucument. The Magna Charta of Indian Philosophy and Religion is and esttablished fact. I would add that it is Universal document of Guidamce for the aspirants and seekers after unmixed bliss and release from the bondage of Samsara and as such it is respected as an unchallenged authority.  
 From the foregoing survey of the Indian Literature, it is paaarent that the Vedas hold a supreme position unchallanged in ectra-sensuous in vestigation. The Charvaka was refuted by the Buddhist and the latter by the Arhatas and Naiyayikas and Vaishnavism joined hands and strengthened the hands of the Vedic school viz., Vedantins, who after refuting all the previous thought-patterns, established the philosophy of the Vedas as the only cooredt philosophy holding the vedas as a book of revelation. Chronologically the Vedantin comes last and holds the ground unquestioned. But propoerly speaking, we need not apply the principle of historical evolution for the domain of metaphysics and philosophy. It is rightly observed by Sri Madhavachargya that all the systems of thoughts are found to exit side by side at all times (अनादिकालतो वृत्ताः समया प्रवाहतः Anuvya. II 2,3); for, thougjt is the mental process, and mind is constituted by three qualiries Satva, Rajas and Tamasm in different proportions according to the nature of the Jiva (Satcik, Rajas and Tamas). These qualities are defined in the Sastras as: one that conduces to the universal good under the command of God is Satvika, that which is destrctive of God's plans embodied in his commands (Vedas) is Tamasa and the middle one is Rajasa. Charvaka is denounced by the Buddhist as a deadly enemy of human good. The Buddhist is condemned as an imperfect thinker and an imposter by the Naiyayikas and Vaiseshikas who in turn are simply speculative and arbitrary in formulating a separate system. Similarly the Sankhyas. Yoga and Mimamskas preach only partial and in some case wrong philosophy. The system of thought based entirely on the Vedas and the auxiliary literature is really the Vedic philosophy called the Vedanta.  
 A cord of explanattion may be put in, about the mature and the charater of the evidence advanced by us in the previous discussion. I have shown that Vedic philosophy is explained by the auxiliary literature i.e. the six Vedangas, the Itihasa, Purana (इतिहासपुराणाभ्यां वेदं समुपबृंहयेत्।). The date and chronology of this evidence does not affect the truth which is not conditioned by space and time. Since human word is subject to the mental and physical defects of perjury, decitfulness etc., it neet not be held as authentic to convey the Truth in entirety unless it is proved to be beyond the influence of all deficiences.  
 A word unaffected by all sorts of deficiencies has to be accepted to exepound the extra-sensuous objects like God, Duty and that is the Vedas which are traditionally known as unblemished by human touch. Next to the Vedas, the Satra texts which are supported by the Vedas are reliable. Such are the works of Sri Vedavyasa (the Avatara of Vishnu) Author of Brahmasutras, Purana, Mahabharata, and Bhagavata etc., as well as the treatises of ऋषि'l like Jaimini, Manu, Yainavalkya etc., In this discussion, we need not enter into the chronology and the original or late texts, interpolations etc., of several literary texts or into the authorship of the works cited above. The Vedantin rests satisfied with the trust worthiness of the Itihas, Puranas etc., cited by him to support the thesis in as much as they are said to be compositions of the ominisciant Vedavyasa, Avatara of God Vishnu. All the Acharyas in their Bhashyas and commentaries trace their philosophy to the Vedas and quote the evidence of the Ithasa and Puranas to support their thesis. This only shows that they held as conclusive the homogenity of the litrary evidences irrespective of their different chronology. Evidence of the contemporary period alone, unless supported by other incontrovertible proof, is not always above suspicion. So it is unfruitful to expend our energies in ascertaining the chronology of a work provided it is composte and conforms to the crtieria of interpretation viz.
उपक्रमोपसंहार etc.  
 The traditional opponents of the Vedas have been refuted by the Vedantin and their philosophy is shown to be quite unsound and unacceptable. The modern oppinents who comprise the orientalists and advocates of social sciences have adopted new methods of research and valuation in the academic and supper-sensuous domain of phliosophy. Their so-called critical apparatus consists of historical method of evolution, from barbarity to the state of civilzation in all channels of human life. This theory of evolution which was pressed into service by Drawin in explaining the physiological changes in an organic body-e.g., from monkey to man is now freely adopted by scholars in explaining the events of history, linguistic changes and progress of social and political institutions. The study of the Vedas by eminent orientalists like Raoth MaXmuller, Whtney, etc., has resulted in treating this ancient literature as the oldest book of History of Aryan life in India after the Indo-Aryans moved to the east after they were separated from the Ind-Europeans whose home lay in the West. The discovery in Sanskrit and the acquaintance of the Vedic literature in the 18th century during the rule of the East India Company introduced a new science of phliology to the Western scholars who found unmistakable similarity between Sanskrit and the classical languages of the West; Greek, Latin, Swiss etc. This similarity connected the two grohps of people in the West and the East as members of the same race race which they called Aryan. Another race, speaking languages quite independent of Sanskrit was designated as Dravidian. Hordes in the East through Turkey, persia, Afganisthan and settled on the banks of the Sindhu and its tributaries. It is in the Punjab where the five great rivers flow that the Aryans composed the hymns of Rig Veda and poured their heart in rapture at the splendid bounty of the Nature's rich scenery. This event they put at B.C.1500, much later than the works of their brethern in the west. This strory of Aryan migration to Bharatavarsha i.e., India is constructed from the study of languages, archaeological and anthropological remains, Socialogy etc, The Vedic literature grew in bulk with the fresh compositions of Aryan Bards composed at different periods of their soujoura in the Gangetic prayers for long and eventful life, rich with material wealth. The Aryans instituted the custom of sacrifices for which the parapharnalia required the services of priests for offering oblation, singing at the alter and for preparation of Vedic sthandilas etc. To suit these subsidiary ceremonies further Vedic psalms came into being. They were known as Yajus, Saman and Atharva-Veda. Future generations which had forgotten the import of these hymns in the influx of time prepared guide books called Vedangas to interpret them, Historical literature recounting the exploits and achievements of old kings and heroes of the Vedic and post Vedie period was composed. These attempts of the poets and bards resulted in the vast literture of the Vedic and post Vedic perods. Since the names of the authors were forgotten in the hoary past, the Vedic literature passed off as unsritten (Apaurusheya). Some of the Vedic hymns still ratain the names of aouthor as Vasistha, Visvamitra, Gritsamada, Kathaka, etc. It is stupid to call them as Apaurusheya in the face of the mention of these names as their authors. It is more than probeble that the Brahmans who held privilged status in the society and were the sole custodians of the Vedas the highest books of knowledge, wanted to retain and aintain unquestioned superioity of their position in the society and contrived to call the Vedas as the commandments of God nver to be tampered with and questioned. The institution of sacrifice is the strong-hold of Brahman aggrandisement. At last a strong revolt was witnessed in India, at the rise of Gautama Buddha Who set at naught the Vedas as the concoetion of Brahman priests, Charvaka and Arhatas followed suit. The Brahmans struggled hadr to mentain their prestige for which they wrote the Mahabharata, Ramayana and a hort of Smriti and Sutra works to cheat the common folk with injuctions of \`do'd and \`not do's for establishing their age-old hold on the society. Thus, the Vedas are nothing but poetic composition and historical documents and the latter literature is the deliberate concoction of priest craft.  
 Maxmuller has earned a distinct honour among the Vedic Scholars of the world by his very learned editions of the Rig Ved edited with enormous care and examination of the Mss. and theis commentaries, constitng their coorect and orginal texts. His study of the Vedas and their commentaries by Sayana is really an astonishing feat especially as he pursused his researches remaining in his own country. The Bhashas of Sayana, the works of Jaimini, Sabara-Bhashya, and kumarila Bhatta's Vartikas and Sayana's exhaustive Bhashya-all of which have with one voive advocated and established the Apaurusheyatva and supreme authority of the Vedas with very convincing array of evidences have unfortuately added coal to his fire of hatred against Brahmans poverty, sacrifice, meditation and due to their self-imposed poverty, sacrifice, meditation and inner vision earned by hard penance and practices.  
 Maxmuller thinks that India had no history until the rise of the Buddhists to chech the agressive priest craft which had cheated the whole society into sub-ordination for long ages. The Vedic Aryans, then rose to their kness and fought hard to maintain their privileged status in the society by their wars with the Kshatriyas e. Parasurama and Dashrathi Rama, and by writing also works of self glorification. The Mahabharata and Ramayana and the Puranas which were purely royal chonicles in their original form underwent a complete overhaul under the Brahmans who transformed then into didactic works preaching philosobhy. Writes he in his \`History of Ancient Sanskrit literature' \`The Indian never knew the felling of nationality, and his heart never trembled in the expection of national applause. There were no heros to inspire a poet no history to call vorth a historian. The only sphere where the Indian Mind found itself at liberty to act, to create and to worship was the sphere of religion and bhilosobhy...But takes as a whole, history supplies no second instance where the inward life of the soul has so completely ablorbed all the practical faculties of the whole people and in fact almost destroyed these qualities by which a nation gains its place in history.... It might therefore be justly said that Indian has no place in the political history of the world (p.16). "The chief elements of discord amongst the peaceful inhabitants of theis rich country were the stuggle for supermacy between the different classes of the society the subjugation of the uncivilized inhabitants, particularly in the south of India, and pressure of the latest comers in the norht upon possissors of the more fertile countries in the south" (p.8-9) The stuggle for supremacy between the different classes which in Greece ended with the downfall of tyrannies and the rising of well-organised republic, has its counterpart in India in the extirpation of the Kshatriya race and the triumph of the Brahmans through Parasurama."  
 Maxmuller indulges in calling Brahmans as "wily Brahaman" and "wily priesthood" and thinks that the women and Shudras were debarred from the study of the Vedas simply to maintain their hollow superiority and control among the masses. Such derogatory observations are obviously the affusion of a poisoned mind and betray the deliberate attempt to suppress the rising spirits of the Hindus. We have no quarrel with Maxmuller or any scholar of the west. We thank them for their hard labour to pulicise the Vedic works by their researches. But, it is the height of ingratitude to the Brahman class (to the Hindus in general) to denounce them as "wily Brahmans" etc. especially as his scholarship and arudition are the gifts of the Brahmans'achievements.  
 We have noted above that all the traditional scholars and Pandits who have studied and written commentaries on the Vedas were impressed by their extra sensuous teachings and declared them as Apaurusheya unblemished supreme authority. They had at their disposal a greater mass of Vedic literature far vaster then that available to midern scholars and their mastery over the meterials was unparalelled. They were aware of the apparently contradictory statements, repetitions, mention of transitory objects, linguistic peculiarities, variety of metres, evoliution of political and administrative systems, and similar other points which the modern orientalists bank upon, for their theory of Aryan migration, chronological strata calling for a slow evution of lingustic patterns and for their conclusion that the Vedas are the most ancient books of Aryan History written at different period, so they cannot be regarded as eternal and spiritual in their contents.  
 The mention of transitory objects like knigs, institutions, customs and practies and place-names, does not affect the eternalness of the Vedas as they are all common names not proper nouns-which abide at all times- past, present and future. Even if they are specific names, as Vasishtha, Visvamitra, etc., they can be accommodated in the vast expanse of time-past, present and future envisaged by the eternal word of the Vedas which is unconditioned by space and time. The sages are the media through whom the eternal word is revealed to the world. Theword may assume different grammatical structures sutited to the time and person though whom it becomes menifest. The God Vishnu becomes majifest in his avataas which take different forms during the Krita, Treta, Dvapara and Kali ages. These forms do not affect in the least. the eternal character of the God. Vishnu in his avateras as Rama, Krishna etc.,is described as child, boy, youth, etc., as if the god is liable to the effects of age god as it the god is liable to the effects of age who transecnds alll the work of Prakriti; i.e., Growth, decay, death ect., Similarly the Vedas stand apart beyond the range of material effects caused by Prakiti.  
 Secondly, the names of persons, places etc., mentioned in the Vedas primarily refer to the all pervading supreme God Vishnu and they are secondarily transferred to worldly objects as conclusively proved in the Brahmasutras, in the आनुमानिकाधिकरण, समाकर्षसूत्र, कल्पनोपदेशसूत्र etc. Hence shri Madhvacharya explains the Vedas as meaning three objects: the material (आधिभौतिक), astral (आधिदैव) and spriritual (अध्यात्म) or worldly objects, deities presiding over them and the Supreme God controlling the Universe see in the अन्तरधिकरण, अन्तर्याम्यधिकरण and अभिमान्यधिकरण of the Brahma Sutras. If we interpreat the Vedas as books of history, we would be ignoring the very function and aim of the vedic literature. Its is quite superficial to stop with the materialistic interpretation and what special purpose would be served by them so as to be regarded by the philosophers as supreme authority for supernatural objects. The dictum परोक्षप्रिया इव हि देवा अपरोक्षद्विषः। (Gods chose to remain obsure and hate publicity) is fully significatiant in the case of the Vedas which contain hidden meaning but appear to outward sight as quite commen place. The examples of Krishna and Rama are quite pertinent to illustrate the statement. To a superficial observer, Krishna is just a man. He expects and attributes all human deficiencies to him. But a man with deep insight into scriptural evidence understands him as God and brushes aside all apparernt defects as meaningless in the context. The most elevated souls in the evoltionistic stage interpret the Vedas by the minute etymological method of पदसमन्वय and conceive every syllable as meaning god Vishnu where-as the ordinary souls seek the wordly as well as trancendental sense by वाक्यसमन्वय. Here three stages are noticed: आध्यात्मिक (Godward,) आधिदैविक (presiding deities over insentient objects). आधिभौमिक (worldly). So, Agni, means fire, presiding deity over insentient fire element (Mahabhuta) and the foremost controlling power, God Vishnu. So there is absolutely no difficulty in accommodating the non-eternal objects in the eternal Vedas. Yaska, Jaimini and Kiumarila Bhatta have explained, as stated in the Sayana-Bhashya on Rig Veda I, बवर, प्रावाहणि as stated terms signifying Vayu who is eternal. I would like to draw the attention of the reader to the famous Puranjanopakhyana story of puranajana as narrted in the Bhagavat IV Skandham whose inner meaning refers to the jouney of the soul towards eternal bliss. But outwardly, it is the history of a certain king Puranjana. This enigma is explained in the same Purana by Narada to Prachinabarhishi. God's creation is mysterious. The human body is the microcosm of cosmos. It contains the entire universe of five elements,: sters, plants, mountains, rivers and every part of the outer world. It is now scientifically proved that even a molecule contains the whole universe. His universe which is real and true in all respects, exemplifies the abstract truths of phliosophy. So the Mahabharata is both Satra and Charitra of Itihas. It is not an allegory of fiction as some would understand it. It is true history which illustrated the permanent truths of phliosophy. The Mahabharata which is regarded as fifth Vedas, is said to yield ten meanings (त्र्यर्थतां श्रुतिषु दशार्थं भारतं ननु) while the Veda proper which is the source of all knowledge is not doubt capable of yielding several meanings simultaneously. Similarly, the whole of Mahabharata is interpreted as containing three meanings-Outward, Inner and Inner most. See भारतार्थस्रिधा प्रोक्तः। and मन्वादि केचिद् ब्रुवते ह्यास्तिकादि तथापरे। तथोपरिचराद्यन्ये भारतं परिचक्षते। where मन्वादि, आ-स्तिकादि and उपरिचरादि---------------------------------represent three layers of senses. Here one point deserves to be noted. The old revilers of the Bedas could be silenced easily by Sastraic arguments under the four corners of logic. But the wild stories of Aryan migiration, evolution of ideas and chronological have invented to satify their pre-conceived notions about the Aryan problem etc., are mere speculations and can be compared with the attacks of Guerilla warfare which does not respect the accepted code their incoherent ravings and thoughtless advances except their own madness turing into sanity and stupdidity of the unbridled resoning in the domain of extra sensuous of the unbridled reasoning in the domain of extra sensuous objects into respect for blanced logic. I have said that the line of argument of the orientalist in respect of the Aryan migration, the charater of Vedas, theory of evolution, similarity of language and mention of historical and gragraphica names in the Vedas etc., is far from convincing, being illogical, speculative and arbitrary. Further there is no consensus of opinion among the orientalists themselves on these problems, each holding quite an opposite view of the other. This circumstance alone is enough to show that their surmises cannot be accepted as final and they are bound to remain inconclusive since surmises have no basw to stand upon (तर्काप्रतिष्ठान्तदन्यथाप्यनुमेयं।). Let me elucidate my point by a few examples:-  
 Archeologists alwats start with the presumption that civilization must have a beginning in babarity. Palaeolithic man was a wandere for food, naked, with no clothes to cover his body. He knew no domestic utensils expcept erude flints to cut the forest yields-fruit, nuts etc. In course of time, he discovered better mode civilized age called Neolithic. He knew no metal, no corporate life and had no sense of civics. slowly he learnt to manufacture iron and bronze and after several thousands of years, he began to build cities and live in fortified towns. He came into contact with foreign civilized nations and learnt many arts, built sanctuaries for Gods and developed abstract thinking which could be called philosophy. India shows all these stages of archarology in the ancient sites excavted so far. The Indus Valley excavations have ushered of India. But this story cannot be accepted. For there is no one opinion about the character of its findings-each excavator-Archarologist, differing from the other. If one calls it Dravidian-proto-dravidian, Pre-Aryan etc. the other finds in the relies purely Aryan, Vediv and Indigenous, culture. I would invite the readers' attention to "The Vedic Age (Bharatiya Vidyabhavan, Bombay) Chapter IX,-The Indus Vally civilization and Chapter X-The Aryan problem. In the preface to the volume, the general editor Dr.R.C.Muzumdar observes" Similarly there is a divergence of opinion regarding the question whether the Indus Valley civilization was pre-Aryan or post-Vedia. In the present state of our knowledge, ne dogmatic answer can be gicen to the questions, and there is no theory that is likely to meet with general acceptance. Even our own contribtors do mnot agree in these points. Dr.Pusalkar who has written on the Indus Valley Civilzation, is inclined to regard it as not fundamentally different from the Aryan, and possible posterior to Rig Vedic culture, while Dr.B.K.Ghosh and Dr.S.K.Chatterji who have written on the Aryan and pre-Aryan peopletake the opposite view (p. 25-26).  
 The examination of pottery, bones, Terracotta articles and fine ornaments unearthed at the Indus Valley sited has not yieded any definite results.  
 It is wrong to presume that the Vedas are the books of the Aryans and that the Aryan and Dravidian-names newly imported into the academic world by the western scholars-orientalists were races antagonistic to each other. The Vedas are universal documents revealed to the Rishis. Whattever be the age of the Rishis to whom they become manifest, the Vedic Syllables, words, sentences etc-their order and sense being immutably fixed are not conditioned by the limitations of time and space. It is a scientific truth that sound and syllables are eternal (nitya). The Vedic sound and cord are divine and distint from the profance word which also is eternal. To tag on the Vedas to the Aryans (as defined by the modern Orientalists) and then fix up their chonology by the so called history of the Aryan as made out by archarologists is a novel attempt of these scholars to condemm these books of knowledge as unauthentic, on the ground of their being works of different authors of different periods. Aryan is not race. Arya is defind as -----as a person of rigid austerity, Satvik, learned and were unatteched to worldly pleasures. Such noble persons were the Brahmans who observed and practised Vedic infunctions strictly. But the Dravida is only a geographical term and does not refer to the race ot language. Shri Krishna declares in the Bhagavadgita that there are only two reces Daiva and Asura-spiritual (Divine) and Materislistic (Asura). (द्वौ भऊतसर्गौ लोकेऽस्मिन् दैव आसुर एव च।) Prahlada a son of Daityaf Hiranya Kashipu was Daiva being the devotee of Vishnu narasinha.  
 Maxmuller's stricture against the Brahmans has no ground to stand upon. Brahman never chose a life of comfort and pleasure. His daily routine was a hard couse of penance, strict discipline in matters of wordly life diet, continence and self-sacrifice. He strove hard for God-cision, abandoned home, family and friends and dedicated himself to medition. He never aspired for honour, superiority or special privileges. Such a powerful stalwart person of high spiritual evolution natually commanded respect and recerence in the Society. He never aspired for honour, superiority ot special privileges. Such a powerful stalwart person of high spiritual evolution natually commanded respect and reverence int he Society. He also spent his energies for the uplift of the uninitned and unevolved or less evolved people. He lived in poor huts in the forest and turored thousands of pulis in all sciences. It is due to the penance of Rishis of hoary antiquIty that Indian still has a never-fading store of spiritual glow. Maxmuller remarks that this spirit of renunciation preached by Brahmins, turned Indian into a country of cowards without a semblance of valour to raise a finger of protest aginst the enemies or wield fiery arms of destruction to check the onslaught of invading mauraders. So, India has no political history to instil pride among the people. It has not carried war expeditions against the foreign kingdoms like Alexfander. We harkten to cooect him and proclaim here that the vedas are not the property of Brahmans, They are the universal strore-house of knowledge in which competent persons are entitled to participate. The competence is judged by the stage of ecolution which one has reached, by the criteria fixed by the Sruti itself. Further, it is historical untruth to think that India had no brave warriors and not countries on military expenditions. Her military and political influnce in the ancient east and west is proved by unquestionable evidence of epigraphy and literature.  
 We need not plead for anybody. History itself is an unimpeachable evidence. What is History ? It is not the parade of short-lived military glory or ill-got victory or of war spoils got by the massacre of innocent men and animals on the battle field. This does not lead us an inch ahead in our journey towards eternal happiness. The western nations which are built up on the wars and butchery of human lives are immersed in the mossy labyrinth of political and social conflicts and religious crusades earred against the Church the citadel of faith and religion. The interneeine wars waged in England, France, Spain, Portugal and Germany originated in the revolt against catholic Church organised by Martin Luther and his followers, left a lasting mark on the life and charavter of the European, blasting his finer glossy nerves of godliness and religious life. Then followed the age of Scientifec inventions and industrialisation which sapped and dried up the sublime ebb of his heart. There was none to check his way ward career. The Church was completely pulled down and suborinated to the popular whims and royal fret and frown. It was in this godless atmosphere of hectic competition that the western mind indulged in the external socialogical resarches and the outcome was the discovery of Darwinism and other social scienced. Christianity which was originally a theistic religion was now wedded to stark science and material prosperity. It was under this uncholesome influence that brilliant oriental scholars like Roth, Weber, Grassman, Biibler, Maxmuller, Grierson, Baldwell, Kittle etc., were bred up and trained and the result is that their works are, for from being objective, marked by the tenour of personal hatred against A God and religion, malice and jealousy, undivine and materialistic outlook. This undivine and aimless enquiry, they call an impartial and objective research. But in India, inspite of mishaps and heretic faith a strong religious hand of saints and philosophers who had imbibed the spirit of the Vedas, controlled the destinies of the kings and the common man and averted the catstrophe. It never allowed them to err from the wholesome spiritual path which ensured hatmony and peace to mankind. If history means rebellion, war, conflict and chaos, India would feign welcome it and be a party to it. Dharma, Artha, Kama and Moksha should be the guiding poles of peogressive life and if one is divorced from the other, ruin and destruction are proper order well-balanced, in India so as to ensure complete harmaony and peace which are essential for real progress. There is absolutely no motive of self aggrandisement and suppression of women and other sections of the society, tn assigning different duties to different groups of people as alleged by maxmuller and his followers.  
 As I have already stated, the Vedas-Brahmanas, Aranyakas and the Upanishads are not historical chronicles nor are they the poetical compositions of literary genius like those of Kalidasa and Bharavi. They are the God's commands transmitted to the sages for the good of His entire creation, at different times and places, unconditioned by the limitations of time and space. They are co-exstent with God without which we cannot dive into the realms beyond the zone of senses and inferences. It is a pity that the orientalists have missed to understand the import of the Vedas and reduced them to the dry routine diaries of an itinerary recording the dates of his travel, the food he ate, the travels, It they had been mere history books of the modern standard or bunches of lyrics and odes recorded nobody would have cared to preserve them through long ages with sancity unknown to other categoy of written literature. Their words, sensesm accents and even the sequence and order of letters used therein, are quite immoutable, separate and distingulished from profane literature: the Sutra, Itihasa, Purana and Kavyas. Such a revered store-house of knowledge is thrown out and dragged into streets mercilessly to seek its own place in the ranks of tales and fables. As I have already mentioned, these scholars have adduced in their support the evidence of archaeology, anthropology, sociology, geology, linguistics, phiology and all sorts of \`logies' prove that the Vedas furnish the history of the most ancient peoples the Aryans. Archaology, on its Aryan problem and Vedic chronolog. Linguistics and phiology which find similarties between the Vedic Sanskrit and the European classical languages have not been able to fix up the evolution of from and sense of words common to both. Further, ther is no telling evidence to determine the course of migration of the Aryans from west to est or from east to west. The cuneiform inscrption at Boxugan mentioning the Vedic deitias and Iranean gods as witnesses of treaty is supposed to lend support to their thery of Aryan migration from the west to the east. But since according to their settled on the banks of the Sindhu and the five tributaries, how can the Vedic deities be mentioned in a record from the western reion(Persia) which the Aryans had left long before they composed the Rig veda in Sind. It at all they had migratted, they must have done so from India long after the composition of the Vedic hymns and laft the Vedic traditions on the way at Persia, Turkley etc. so theat the Vedic deities could be invoked as witnesses of the treaty in the record. Further, philology and Linguistics can be pressed into service by both the perties with equal force, withour coming to any conclustion. The slow evolution of the linguistic forms and senses from epoch to epoch is adduced as a powerful argument to prove the chronological sequences in the Vedic literature. This is called historical linguistics which, the moderns say, was not known to the ancient grammarians of India. True, Panini does not recognise such an evolution, though he knew it , as it is unscientific and cannot be sustained by the philosophy of language. A cord is capable of several meanings by the same vritti or by different vrittis शक्ति, (inherent power), लक्षणा-गौणी etc.(secondary power) and all the shadas of meanings of vration. It is due to several circumstances-ignorance, want of training, local and social contacts, food and elimate and similar couses, that a particular sense sticks on and persists in certain reginons or groups of persons wheras the same word conveys a different sense altogether elsewher. This linguistic problem is discussed in Yasks's Nirukta, Jaimini's Mimamsa Sutrs, Patanjali's Mahabhashya ans other grammatical works. The Vedantis hold that all the sense of words are inherently connected with it and are current simulianeously in the contemporary period and so they quote the evidence of lexicons like Amara, Visva etc., to explein the technical terms occurring in the Vedas and the Sutras. How can a late lexicon be cited to procce the sense of ancient text? This is replied that the words convey all possible senses and all of them may be grasped by the highly evoved souls like Brahma and the eternal word of the Vedas if eternally contacted with all its senses. But, only a limited number of meanings is know to the less evolved persons. Hence, the science of atymology has attained the status of वेदांग in India. Yaska's Nirukta gives several meanings to words in the Nighantu. This solves all the objections of the orientalists against linguistics and semantics. All tenses and moods are current at all times. But only a few of them are found to be in use by persons in certain localities due to various causes.  
 The Vedas are revealed to the sages who have attained a particular stage in spiritual evolution, such sages may be found at all times and in all places.  
 विंशल्लक्षणतोऽनूनस्तपस्वी बहुवेदवित्।  
 वेद इत्येव यं पश्येत्स वेदो ब्रह्मदर्शनात्।  
 Vedas becom manifest to a person who is endowed with twenty qualities (out of 32 which signify the full blown intellect), is well-versed in many Vedas and is a Tapasvin and leads a religious life.  
 The historical details, geographical name of mountains, rivers, towns and villages, administrative information about Corporate bodies, villages, administrative information about the Coporrate bodies, village and city councils and methods of justice, punishment of criminals etc.-these and similar descriptions occurring in the Vedas, Brahmans Aranyakas and Upanishads, point to the surmise that the Society represented by these detailos must refer to different chronological phases. Ture, but sice, as we have already observed, the Vedas are primarily spiritual documents recording the general principles which can be applied to specitic cases at all times successfully, these details signify only the general features of the Society which are true for all times. Yaska and Jaimini suggest a similar explanation in the Nirukta and Mimamsa Sutras respectivly.  
 But in as much the whole of Vedic literature is regarded as a Book of Revelatio-not composed by any person, this historical narration has to be explained in consonance with this age-long tradition Otherwise, how can the wise men's tradition of non-composition of the Vedas be explained ? It is, otherwise, a mystery that the Brahmans and Upanishads are treated as revelations whereas the works ? This riddle is easily solved. This Vedic literature-Mantra, Brahmana-Aranyaka-Upanishad-stands apart from the profane, in that it is entirely divine in its from and sense. It would be unfair and unscientific to compare them with profane literature and trace the course of evolution of form the ideas as is done by some scholars old and new. We quote here an illusration to clarigy our point. Though Lord Krihna and Rama etc., appear as human beings to all out-ward view, similar to the common man like Dittha (or Arjuna and Akrura etc.) the former, being the Avatara of Vishnu is unaffected by the effects of Prakriri: waste, growth, destruction etc., wheras the othe men and women are subject to these changes. Only a person with spirtual outlook and deep faculty of introspection can grasp and appreciate this explanation, Similarly the Vedic word-accent, syllable, sequence, order etc. and its sense are not subject to any changes like the profane word etc., and it is inmutably and permanently fixed in its form and sense. It is as divine and unchangeable as God Vishnu. But since is (Veda) is insentient like primordial matter (Prakriti), it cannot work independently, but functions only under the command of the supreme Soul (Vishnu) on the analogy of द्रव्यं कर्म च कालश्च स्वभावो जीव एव च। यदनुग्रहतः संति न सन्ति यदुपेक्षया॥ (All eternal objects function under the will of God. Such an explanation may be unconving to the modern scholars whose standards of judgement are materialistic and physical. Since the vedas are in a sense coterminous with the God. (whose existence cannot be denied) and are His commands resting i His Mind during Pralaya or period of Dissolution (ईशबुद्धिस्थिताः।) since also in God's cration nothing is new, every thing is per-determined-an extension of its old proto-type (धाता यथा पूर्वमकल्पयत्) since also all names and objects do exist in their unmanifest forn, they we become manifest in due course of the evolution and then we become conscious of these names and objects as historical events. The Vedas being linitless (अनंता वै वेदाः) and all-pervading like God Vishnu, they at the will of the latter, flash to certain souls whose evolutionistic degree is so great as to be competent to attract the sound waves of the Vedic words which are all-prevading. At that moment the personal names, names of mountains, rivers of the political or social transactions (mentioned in the Vedas) are reflected on the mental plane of the seer. The so-called past, present, future tenses and moods and voices are one sheet of Present Tense and Active Voice in God's mind, and to us they are converted into different tenses and moods. It is a matter of great surprise to us to know that astrology, an imperfect science though, reads the past, present and future events to certain extent. The Ashta Siddhis (eight miracular accomplishments) show wonderful achievements of human mind. So, the mention of these physical, mental and historical particulars in the Vedas has to be explained only as common names. They are let down to the mental plane of the Rishis-they being only transmitters, and not creators, in proper terminology and language suited to the time. For, God's commands are not of one of one order and linguistic pattern. Rig Veda is accented, the other Vedas are not. Some are in Anushtubh and highly evolved metres and others are not., Compare for example, the revolutions of a constant picture film or Radio talk which throws to view its contents at fined intervels. So, the which throws to view its contents at fined intervels. Som the peculiarties of language and metre may be explained away thus, satisfactorily.  
 We cannot treat the Vedas as compositions-prose or poetry, of persons enchanted by the beauty of nature or immersed in the sacerdotal rituals, seeking worldly comforts. Such works cammot command implicit reverence from all sections of people as distinguished from the Smiritis of Manu or the Kavyas of poets, Kalidasa etc. We have already denounced the theory of Brahman's wily motivity advanced by the moderns, as unworthely of consideration.   
 Futher,the supposition that the primitive man started his career in barbarity and slowly moved towards civilization is also contary to evidence, since from the remotest antiquity, hisstory demonstrates the truth of gradation among souls and gradual evolution according to their respective capacities. Archaeology, Anthtopology, Sociology etc., are imperfect in their results. They can dive into the past for a few thousands of years only that too vaguely. But the origin of earth and other planets of the God's creation goes back to several aeons of ages in unending cycles until the full evolution of souls in the respective Ages (kalpa) and the materials ate buried in the womb of the earth thrown pellmell due to volcanic eruptions, earth-quakes and deluge etc, without any order or sequence so as to indicate their chronological strata. Further, the examination of these relics has landed the invesstigators in utter chaos and confusion. The several criteria of C-14 test and Acid test etc., used by the Archaelolgisits to fix up the age of the finds are found to be defective and unreliable. Similarly all other sciences like anthropology etc., have failed to give unquestionable conclusions. Thus, these experimantal sciences on which the modern schjolarship is based have done more harm than good in the academical and extra sensuous fields during the last 200 years all the world over and the man's energies are wasted over such unfruitful pursuits. The Hindu mind which directed its capacities towards the solution of the God's mystery in search of permanent happiness has now become sterile and barren with worthless invesigations.  
 It is claimed by the Western scholars that "a qualified European is better able to arrive at the true meaning of the Rigveda than a Brahman interpreter. The Judgement of the former is unfettered by theological bias. He possesses the historial faculty and he has also a far winder intellectual horizon., equipped as he is with all the resources of scientific scholarship. Roth, therefore, set himsely to compare carefully all passages parallel in from and matter, with due regard to considerations of context, grammar and aty mology while consulting, though, prerhaps, with insufficient attentiom the traditional interpretations. He thus subjected the Rigveda to a historical tretment within the range of Sanskrit itself. He further called in the assistance rendred from without, by the comparative method, utilising the helpo afforded not nony by the Avesta, which is so closely allied to the Rig veda in language and matter, but also by the results tof comparative philology, resources unknow to the trsditional scholar".  
 -A History of Sanskrit Literatur by  
  Arthur A.Macdonall, P.57  
   
 Wee are quite of the hard labours of the Western scholars in interpreting the Vedas and also their inability to understand their import correctly. We are happy to record here that the criteria of interoretation followed by the traditional Bhashyakaras and commentators in India are far nore digid, appropriate and free from flaws. These are drawn from the deep study of the whole mass of literature with a view to establishing the homogenutiy of meaning and purport of the texts under study. A perusal at the Mimamsa manual would convince even a fastidious critic, of the correctness of the precautions takes by the ancient authors against the usual pitfalls and errors of superficial interpreters. Before undertaking to write the Completed with strict adherence to rigid scrutiny:-  
 (1) qualifications of the commentators.  
   
 (2) collection of manuscripts and collation of different readings in different recensious.  
   
 (3) Fixing up the reading which would satisfy the subject matter of the work, intended by the author.  
   
 (4) Impartial and objectve approach to the study
